Oh, my sons, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last part of the science of medicine, and its completion has achieved its purpose in me, and through its explanations and declarations, it seems to me that you should take care to keep this treatise, which was divided from surgery with me.
For surgery with me is so rare in our region and in our time, that it has almost lost its science, and its practice is forgotten; and there remain from it only some little descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been changed much and added to those errors and conjectures that were hidden among their intentions, and its force and art have been stretched out.
And it seems to me that you have brought the practice of this treatise back to life with its orderly arrangement, according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools of the craft may be added thereto, and prepared for use, which is necessary.
But the reason why no skilled craftsman in their own hand is found in our time is that the art of medicine is long and requires its practitioner to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which Guillaume knew well in so far as he understood the joints of the members and their forms, and the connection and separation of them; and had knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, and their number, and the arrangement of them; and the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of their effluence.
And for this reason says Hippocrates that in a short name there is great thought, especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of this in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about anatomy will be led into error by which men will die, just as I have seen many of them, for some are trained in this science and yet leave it for another science and experiments.
For you saw a foolish surgeon who had attempted to excise an abscess on the neck of a woman and had cut into some arteries in the neck, causing much blood to flow before the woman died.
And I saw another doctor who had operated on a man in his estate, and the stone was large, and had come to him and taken that stone out with a piece of the bladder, so that the man died on the third day.
And I had already predicted that he would flee away from there, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, it was evident that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving payment from the Duke of our land for surgery, and he undertook to treat a blacksmith whose leg was fractured. And due to his ignorance, he removed the splinter from the fracture, put plasters and sticks with great tension on top of the wound, and did not allow it to breathe.
And bind the ligaments separately, according to their desires, and reapply the dressing, and leave it loose for some days and command that we loosen the bandage; and thus it should be that the space and the flesh were originally attached, and come back to their proper condition.
And I was called to him, and I prepared myself to loosen the bandage, and he obtained his calmness and began to be less troubled by his pains.
But however the corruption was already confirmed in the member, so that I could not hold it back, and the corruption did not stop roaming in the member until the patient became perilous.
And I saw another physician who pierced an infected cancerous swelling, and it was ulcerated within some days, until the wickedness of him and his lord were magnified.
This is because the black dog (a metaphor for melancholy or evil) is pure in its humor, and it's not necessary that it should be cured with every kind of iron (i.e., medical treatment), but rather it should be left as a member which suffers from being tormented.
And for this reason, sons, it is necessary that the operation be divided into two parts: one in which health is associated with him, and another work in which danger is present in great dispositions.
And I have already said this in every place of this book where the operation is one in which there is error and fear; for it is necessary that you guard against this and leave those who are not worthy, so that the leaves may not be troubled to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore take your arms with supplication and protection of God, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
And use the best means for the sake of God to attain salvation and glorious success, and drive out the terrible illnesses with difficult cure, and stop using those weapons from which you fear, so that your situation in your faith and in your name does not escape: because it remains more to your glory, and also in the world and finally to your sanctity.

The quality of the joints formed by this cautery and its scars, and in what condition is cautery prohibited.
So I say that the discourse about the quality of the joints formed by cautery and its scars is long and prolix, subtle for knowledge, and secretly hidden; and already many wise men have spoken of it, and they are in disagreement among themselves, and I am afraid of prolonging it further.
And so I say that cautery agrees universally with all conditions of matter or its material, except for two conditions, which are scorching states without material.
In the hot and dry condition with no material there will be desiccation; for some have said that cautery is beneficial in this case, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable in a disease which is of quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inappropriate that a hot and dry condition with water should be healed by something that is also hot and dry.
And I reply to him who said the opposite, that by cautery is made a good joint in all hot and dry diseases that are found in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and its humors with the condition of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say by the word of him, that through experience I have already many times discovered.
When however it is not necessary that the one who has already been experienced and exercised in the capital of cauterization by a final exercise, and who knows the diversity of human complexion and the disposition of illnesses in their own persons, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the space of time of those, should come upon this.
However in other complexions it is not to be feared, and most especially in the humid and wet illnesses, because all doctors are already agreed on these, and there is no discord among them about judgment by cauterization in these.
And you know, sons, that from the secret of healing by cauterization with fire and from its goodness, it is on cauterization that medicine counteracts, because fire is simple, whose action reaches only the member which is cauterized and does not harm another member placed nearby, except for a small damage.
However, the action of counteracting medicine reaches as far as those members which are distant from it, and it quickly brings a difficult-to-cure illness to the affected member, and it does so swiftly.
However, fire, due to its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does not act on the outer layer but only on what is superfluous. And it has already been known to me through experience and the length of my service in studying this art, that it is true about the causes; and for this reason I am excused from the length of this sermon. But if I did not have permission to write down a secret hidden in fire and the quality of its operation on bodies and its expulsion by which it drives out illnesses, using a philosophical demonstrative sermon, which would be suitable for your souls.
And you should know, my sons, that the seasons are not in harmony when it is advisable to make a cauterization and when the best time of spring has passed.
And I say that cauterization is advisable at all times, because the damage caused by the accidental passing of time is submerged in the effect of the liquid which has the cauterization attached, and most especially if the cauterization is for pains or necessary and severe pains, which do not suffer delay, whereas those that come with bad omen are feared to be greater than small harm caused by time.
And, I say, that is not what the physicians think, my sons, for they do not value this method except among the common people and foolish doctors; indeed, in that illness which is cured by cauterization it does not diminish with time, and its consequences remain.
And the cause is not so easy as they think, because cauterization is nothing but a place of medicine which alters the composition and dries out the humors which are the cause for the pains to come.
But, nonetheless, cauterization is an excess over medicine, sought for the sake of its utility and virtue of its operation, and the greatness of its lord.
It is possible that his illness may return at some hour of time, according to the constitution of the patient and the location of their illness, and virtue in them, and what is prepared in their body from the aggregation of superfluities in them, and what has been acquired by them in foods and appearances of those causes; but since the illness which is administered cauterization is a subtle disease in few members and humidity, such as tooth cauter for pain and similar to that, it is possible that in him that pain will not return, but that will be done in small things.
And in plain language it is said that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, and it is an unjust statement, not like what I understand in it, because I believe it is not a cure that benefits with medicine or any other cause appropriate to cauterization.

On Cauterization of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted to the inner parts and strike the eye.
When the eyelashes are converted to the inner parts and strike the eye so that they puncture it, you can cauterize them in two ways: either with fire or with a burning medicine.

Chapter XIII.
Concerning the cure of an abscess which appears on the upper eyelid.
When an abscess appears on the eyelid and is a contraction of the eyelid when it is narrowed to one side or the other due to poor healing of a wound, incision, or cauterization, and is called leporina, and this abscess can be either natural or accidental, and is caused by the healing of a wound, incisions, or cauterizations, or resemblance to them.
The manner of the operation on it is that you cut through that consolidation and separate its edges, and place a piece of linen cloth in between them, and tie those edges together so they may be healed.
And it is not advisable to apply a poultice or dressing to it from the causes that dry and constrict, for if you do so, the abscess will return worse than ever, and at no time have I seen it improve.
Use in it the causes that moisten and soften, such as fenugreek, and mix with water in which you boil a sprig of it or its seeds, or with aquilonic ointment, which is liquefied with some oil, and immerse the cloth in it, and cure with it.
And the treasure of your treatment is that you pierce through all the thickening that has not consolidated according to its original form. (This means that you should carefully and gently cut or puncture the abscess, but only if it has not already healed properly and formed a solid scab.)
And this operation that we have described is nothing but a correction of something that has formed incorrectly and does not return to its original shape. (This means that the procedure is aimed at restoring the natural form or appearance of the affected area, which had been distorted by the abscess.)

Splinters come in different varieties according to the species and the locations of the bodies they affect, because their diversity lies in the fact that some of them have large points, small ones, concave ones, dull ones, which are solid; and among others there are those with three angles, and among others tongues-shaped ones, and among others forked ones.
And the symptoms of the splinter that affects the brain are when it pierces the bone and settles in the cranium, which is above the brain, causing severe headache, scotoma (blindness or loss of vision), dizziness, tremors in the hands, inflammation and numbness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of thought, vomiting with bile, and in severe cases, the person's speech becomes slurred and their voice is destroyed. Additionally, a white, dusty-like fluid comes out of the wound, similar to pus, and the surrounding flesh appears swollen, as if it were filled with liquid.

There are various types of dislocations that occur due to a blow or fracture, or in any other way.
When any of these causes occur, and you puncture in the treatment of it or in its recovery, very often such things will happen as death.
And therefore it is not fitting that anyone, other than the one who is skilled in the art, with long experience, mercy, and piety, should take charge of his treatment, unless he is bold, hesitant or presumptuous; but use, at the beginning of medicines, those which have proved themselves safe, and less likely to harm the patient, rather than those to which you hope for salvation from death, alleviation of illness, and in which there appears any hope. And then try to reduce the swelling from him as soon as possible at the beginning of the cause, before it turns into a hard abscess.
And then, if the limb returns to its normal state as we wish, administer a regimen that will reduce the hard abscess and cure the wound with water or dry plaster dressings as are suitable for him.
And if the dislocation is with a fracture and the splinters of bone are separated, then you must perforate the space between them, and do what we have said about simple fractures, where it has been mentioned in their places.
And guard and avoid, as befits your virtue, that of the instrument in the ways of fear, according to what has preceded my preaching to you; for this is more becoming to your Creator, and more lasting to your glory, and more salvation to your true body in your time. Amen. (Note: The text ends with a traditional phrase "Ayssi finieso..." which translates to "Thus I end...") In the name of God, a prayer or an invocation is often used to begin a medieval medical text.
